<span id="freeTextContainer3030267123239264962"><em>Librarian Note: This edition's ISBN is in conflict with another's in the database - <a title="The Vines in Splendour" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23997102.The_Vines_in_Splendour">The Vines in Splendour</a>.</em><p>Sometimes a man needs help learning to be a dad,,,That's what Daddy School is all about.</p><p> <strong>Twin Tornadoes!</strong> </p><p>Seven-year-old dynamos Erin and Sean are single father Dennis Murphy's pride and joy. Even though they're bank robbers. But Dennis is the best damn lawyer in Arlin</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3030267123239264962"><em>Librarian Note: This edition's ISBN is in conflict with another's in the database - <a title="The Vines in Splendour" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23997102.The_Vines_in_Splendour">The Vines in Splendour</a>.</em><p>Sometimes a man needs help learning to be a dad,,,That's what Daddy School is all about.</p><p>
  <strong>Twin Tornadoes!</strong>
</p><p>Seven-year-old dynamos Erin and Sean are single father Dennis Murphy's pride and joy. Even though they're bank robbers. But Dennis is the best damn lawyer in Arlington, and, after all, they were only unwitting accomplices. So when his legal opponent Gail Saunders suggests that his kids are less than perfect, she becomes more than his professional enemy.</p><p>Trouble is, Gail's as tenacious as the twins. She's not going to give up until she's won her case - and her point. She challenges Dennis to a course at the Daddy School to prove once and for all who's the better parent, even though she doesn't have kids of her own. Yet.</p><p>It's a no holds barred contest, and the winner takes all...</p></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1033344551">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1033344551" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13519125-terri" class="left imgcol" title="Terri"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1432661746p2/13519125.jpg" alt="Terri" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1033344551?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13519125-terri" class="user" title="Terri">Terri</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1033344551">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8410682996695364645"> Another great hit for Judith Arnold!<br /> 1st let me say, I read / listened to this book in audio format via audible.com. This whole Daddy School series is a perfect set for audiobooks as when combining the humor of the author and the narrators voices / accents, makes it loads of laughs. I love audiobooks! <br /> Book 3, Father of 2, is a take off from the 1st book Father Found (the part when 2 seven-year olds were caught helping rob an ATM). Here we meet with the father of these 2 kids, who happens to be</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8410682996695364645"> Another great hit for Judith Arnold!<br /> 1st let me say, I read / listened to this book in audio format via audible.com. This whole Daddy School series is a perfect set for audiobooks as when combining the humor of the author and the narrators voices / accents, makes it loads of laughs. I love audiobooks! <br /> Book 3, Father of 2, is a take off from the 1st book Father Found (the part when 2 seven-year olds were caught helping rob an ATM). Here we meet with the father of these 2 kids, who happens to be a lawyer. With these 2 kids, everyday is an adventure. The kids (twins) are wise beyond their years &amp; very funny! Dennis meets Molly (lawyer for opposing side) and sparks start to fly. While Dennis &amp; Molly do the "lets avoid dating thing" dance, Dennis's twins keep us entertained. Thru Molly, we meet Leo, a Russian transient who has trouble understanding the American language which makes this book even funnier with the words he chooses to use. Leo, talk Molly into suing a newspaper and the story unfolds from there.<br /> Of all 3 books in this series, I loved this book the most! The twins are so funny. They are wise for their age, but they think they know everything. I laughed &amp; laughed through out this book. <br /> The author, Judith Arnold kept me entertained the entire time. I liked this book so much, I read it straight thru in 1 day! Tom Dheere, the narrator, did a fantastic job with all the voices. Tom did a really awesome Russian voice and accent for Leo. it sounded very authentic! Kudos to both Judith &amp; Tom for a job well done!<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8410682996695364645">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_20191752">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20191752" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1082192-kendra" class="left imgcol" title="Kendra"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1213924486p2/1082192.jpg" alt="Kendra" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20191752?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 02, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1082192-kendra" class="user" title="Kendra">Kendra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20191752">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18329168876851560637">This story has as cute premise, but falls victim to the cute kids syndrom. The "cute kids" turn more annoying than cute. I found myself skimming over the kids talking, because they got on my nerves. I kept thinking that the story might have been more interesting with older kids, say about 12 or so. That would have made for some great dynamics with the heroine and possible gf for dad.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7DQcWHd8r/04YWlzK8KPKwW4Qp2ANqLtOMbTjSxGxKSJ4COLha67B7S5HchVo2mZTE+BhMnr5UdSz9Yf4NMy4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36638.Judith_Arnold">About Judith Arnold</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/36638.Judith_Arnold"><img alt="36638" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336490025p2/36638.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer70371124260387245">Barbara Keiler<br />aka <a title="Ariel Berk" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/256303.Ariel_Berk">Ariel Berk</a>, <a title="Thea Frederick" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3206262.Thea_Frederick">Thea Frederick</a>, Judith Arnold<br /><br />Barbara Keiler was born on April 7th. She started telling stories before shecould write. She was four when her sister, Carolyn, stuffed a crayon intoher hand and taught her the alphabet, and she's been writing ever since.<br /><br />Barbara is a graduate of Smith College, where she learned to aim for thestars, and she received a master's degree in cre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText70371124260387245">Barbara Keiler<br />aka <a title="Ariel Berk" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/256303.Ariel_Berk">Ariel Berk</a>, <a title="Thea Frederick" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3206262.Thea_Frederick">Thea Frederick</a>, Judith Arnold<br /><br />Barbara Keiler was born on April 7th. She started telling stories before shecould write. She was four when her sister, Carolyn, stuffed a crayon intoher hand and taught her the alphabet, and she's been writing ever since.<br /><br />Barbara is a graduate of Smith College, where she learned to aim for thestars, and she received a master's degree in creative writing from BrownUniversity, where she took aim at a good-looking graduate student in thechemistry department and wound up marrying him. She says: "Before myhusband and I were married, I had a job in California and he was working onhis Ph.D. in Rhode Island. I became ill, and he hopped on a plane and flewacross the country to be with me. Neither of us had any money, but he saidhe simply couldn't concentrate on his research, knowing I was three thousandmiles away and facing a serious health problem all by myself. He stayed fortwo weeks, until I was pretty well recovered. That he would just drop whathe was doing, put his life on hold and race to my side told me how much heloved me. After that, I knew this was the man I wanted to marry."<br /><br />Barbara has received writing fellowships from the Shubert Foundation and theNational Endowment for the Arts, and has taught at colleges and universitiesaround the country. She has also written several plays that have beenprofessionally staged at regional theaters in San Francisco, Washington, D.C.,Connecticut and off-off-Broadway.<br /><br />Since her first romance novel's publication in 1983 as Ariel Berk. Shewrote one novel as Thea Frederick, and since 1985 she writes asJudith Arnold. Barbara has sold more than 70 novels, with eight millioncopies in print worldwide. She has recently signed a contract with MIRABooks. Her first MIRA novel will appear in 2001. She has received severalawards from Romantic Times Magazine, including awards for the Best HarlequinAmerican Romance of the Year, Best Harlequin Superromance of the Year, BestSeries Romantic Novel of the Year and a Lifetime Achievement Certificate ofMerit for Innovative Series Romance. She has also been a finalist for theGolden Medallion Award and the RITA Award for Romance Writer of America. Hernovel Barefoot in the Grass has appeared on the recommended reading listsdistributed by cancer support services at several hospitals.<br /><br />Barbara lives in a small town not far from Boston, Massachusetts, New England with her husband, two teenage sons, and a guinea pig named Wilbur. Her sister Carolyn died of breast cancer in 1998.</span>
